Question 1easy

The area of a rectangle with length 8 cm and width 5 cm is:

  1. 26 cm²
  2. 40 cm²
  3. 13 cm²
  4. 80 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 40 cm²

Area of rectangle = length × width = 8 × 5 = 40 cm².

Question 2easy

The sum of angles in a triangle is:

  1. 90°
  2. 180°
  3. 270°
  4. 360°
Show answer

Answer: 180°

The sum of all interior angles of a triangle is always 180°.

Question 3medium

Area of sector with radius 14 cm and angle 90° (π=22/7):

  1. 154 cm²
  2. 616 cm²
  3. 308 cm²
  4. 77 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 154 cm²

Area of sector = (θ/360)×πr² = (90/360)×(22/7)×196 = (1/4)×616 = 154 cm².

Question 4easy

If side of cube is halved, volume becomes:

  1. 1/8 th
  2. 1/4 th
  3. 1/2
  4. 1/6 th
Show answer

Answer: 1/8 th

Original V=s³. New V=(s/2)³=s³/8. Volume becomes 1/8th.

Question 5medium

The total surface area of a hemisphere with radius 7 cm (π=22/7):

  1. 462 cm²
  2. 308 cm²
  3. 154 cm²
  4. 231 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 462 cm²

TSA = 3πr² = 3×(22/7)×49 = 3×22×7 = 462 cm².

Question 6medium

A cylinder has radius r and height h. If r is doubled and h is halved, volume:

  1. Doubles
  2. Quadruples
  3. Halves
  4. Same
Show answer

Answer: Doubles

Original V=πr²h. New V=π(2r)²(h/2)=π×4r²×h/2=2πr²h. Volume doubles.

Question 7easy

In triangle ABC, angle A=50°, angle B=60°. Exterior angle at C is:

  1. 110°
  2. 130°
  3. 70°
  4. 120°
Show answer

Answer: 110°

Angle C=180−50−60=70°. Exterior angle at C = 180−70=110°. Also: exterior angle = sum of two non-adjacent interior angles = 50+60=110°.

Question 8medium

If two angles of a triangle are 45° and 75°, the triangle is:

  1. Scalene obtuse
  2. Scalene acute
  3. Isosceles
  4. Right-angled
Show answer

Answer: Scalene obtuse

Third angle=180−45−75=60°. All three angles (45°,60°,75°) are different → scalene. All angles < 90° → acute. So scalene acute.

Question 9easy

A tangent to a circle at point P is perpendicular to:

  1. Radius at P
  2. Diameter
  3. Chord through P
  4. Any line
Show answer

Answer: Radius at P

A tangent to a circle at any point is perpendicular to the radius drawn to that point of tangency.

Question 10easy

In a circle, equal chords are:

  1. Equidistant from center
  2. On same arc
  3. Parallel
  4. Equal in length only
Show answer

Answer: Equidistant from center

Equal chords of a circle are equidistant from the center of the circle (theorem).

Question 11easy

Which set of lengths can form a right triangle?

  1. 6,8,10
  2. 5,10,12
  3. 3,5,7
  4. 4,6,8
Show answer

Answer: 6,8,10

Check: 6²+8²=36+64=100=10². Yes, 6,8,10 is a Pythagorean triple.

Question 12medium

An isosceles triangle has equal sides of 13 cm and base 10 cm. Its area:

  1. 60 cm²
  2. 50 cm²
  3. 65 cm²
  4. 55 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 60 cm²

Height=√(13²−5²)=√(169−25)=√144=12 cm. Area=½×10×12=60 cm².

Question 13medium

The ratio of the volumes of two cubes is 8:27. Ratio of their surface areas:

  1. 4:9
  2. 2:3
  3. 8:27
  4. 16:81
Show answer

Answer: 4:9

Volume ratio=8:27=(a/b)³=8:27→a:b=2:3. Surface area ratio=(a/b)²=4:9.

Question 14medium

A right circular cone has base radius 6 cm and slant height 10 cm. Volume (π=22/7):

  1. 301.71 cm³
  2. 452.57 cm³
  3. 150.85 cm³
  4. 200 cm³
Show answer

Answer: 301.71 cm³

Height=√(10²−6²)=√64=8. V=(1/3)πr²h=(1/3)×(22/7)×36×8=(1/3)×(22/7)×288=(22×288)/21=6336/21=301.71 cm³.

Question 15easy

Area of a triangle with base 12 cm and height 8 cm is:

  1. 48 cm²
  2. 96 cm²
  3. 56 cm²
  4. 40 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 48 cm²

Area = ½×base×height = ½×12×8 = 48 cm².

Question 16easy

Circumference of a circle with radius 14 cm is (π=22/7):

  1. 88 cm
  2. 44 cm
  3. 176 cm
  4. 22 cm
Show answer

Answer: 88 cm

Circumference = 2πr = 2×(22/7)×14 = 2×22×2 = 88 cm.

Question 17medium

A rectangle 20m×15m has a path 2m wide outside. Area of path:

  1. 208 m²
  2. 200 m²
  3. 196 m²
  4. 216 m²
Show answer

Answer: 208 m²

Outer rectangle: (20+4)×(15+4)=24×19=456. Inner=20×15=300. Path area=456−300=156 m². Hmm: 456−300=156. That's not 208. Let me recalculate: 24×19=456, 300. 456−300=156. Not matching options. With path inside: (20−4)×(15−4)=16×11=176. Path=300−176=124. Neither matches. Perhaps path is 2m wide inside: 300−(16×11)=300−176=124. Or outer path: (20+4)(15+4)−300=456−300=156. None of the options. Likely intended: path 2m wide outside: (24×19)−(20×15)=456−300=156≠208. Possible the dimensions are different in intended question.

Question 18medium

A 14m×10m room has a carpet 2m away from walls all around. Carpet area:

  1. 60 m²
  2. 80 m²
  3. 40 m²
  4. 100 m²
Show answer

Answer: 60 m²

Carpet dimensions: (14−4)×(10−4)=10×6=60 m².

Question 19easy

The cost of carpeting a floor 20m×15m at ₹12 per m²:

  1. ₹3,600
  2. ₹3,000
  3. ₹4,200
  4. ₹2,800
Show answer

Answer: ₹3,600

Area = 20×15 = 300 m². Cost = 300×12 = ₹3,600.

Question 20medium

The cost of painting 4 walls of a room 10m×8m×5m at ₹2 per m²:

  1. ₹360
  2. ₹300
  3. ₹400
  4. ₹280
Show answer

Answer: ₹360

Area of 4 walls = 2×h×(l+b) = 2×5×(10+8) = 10×18 = 180 m². Cost = 180×2 = ₹360.

Question 21medium

If ΔABC ~ ΔPQR with BC:QR = 3:4, ratio of their areas:

  1. 9:16
  2. 3:4
  3. √3:√4
  4. 6:8
Show answer

Answer: 9:16

Ratio of areas of similar triangles = square of ratio of corresponding sides = (3/4)² = 9:16.

Question 22easy

A square and a rectangle have equal areas. If square side=12cm and rectangle length=18cm, rectangle breadth:

  1. 8 cm
  2. 6 cm
  3. 9 cm
  4. 10 cm
Show answer

Answer: 8 cm

Square area=144 cm². 18×b=144. b=8 cm.

Question 23easy

Area of a rhombus with diagonals 16 cm and 12 cm is:

  1. 96 cm²
  2. 192 cm²
  3. 48 cm²
  4. 144 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 96 cm²

Area of rhombus = (d₁×d₂)/2 = (16×12)/2 = 192/2 = 96 cm².

Question 24medium

Perimeter of a semicircle of radius 7 cm is (π=22/7):

  1. 36 cm
  2. 44 cm
  3. 22 cm
  4. 30 cm
Show answer

Answer: 36 cm

Perimeter = πr+2r = r(π+2) = 7×(22/7+2) = 7×(22/7+14/7) = 7×36/7 = 36 cm.

Question 25easy

The side of a square whose area is equal to area of a rectangle 8 cm × 18 cm:

  1. 12 cm
  2. 16 cm
  3. 10 cm
  4. 14 cm
Show answer

Answer: 12 cm

Area of rectangle = 8×18 = 144 cm². Side of square = √144 = 12 cm.

Question 26easy

Area of a trapezium with parallel sides 8 cm and 12 cm and height 6 cm:

  1. 60 cm²
  2. 80 cm²
  3. 72 cm²
  4. 90 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 60 cm²

Area = ½×(sum of parallel sides)×height = ½×(8+12)×6 = ½×20×6 = 60 cm².

Question 27medium

If radius of a circle is increased by 10%, its area increases by:

  1. 21%
  2. 10%
  3. 20%
  4. 25%
Show answer

Answer: 21%

New area = π(1.1r)² = 1.21πr². Increase = 21%.

Question 28medium

Area of an equilateral triangle with side 6 cm is:

  1. 9√3 cm²
  2. 12√3 cm²
  3. 6√3 cm²
  4. 18√3 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 9√3 cm²

Area = (√3/4)×s² = (√3/4)×36 = 9√3 cm².

Question 29easy

The diagonal of a square is 10√2 cm. Its area is:

  1. 100 cm²
  2. 200 cm²
  3. 50 cm²
  4. 150 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 100 cm²

Diagonal = s√2 = 10√2. s = 10 cm. Area = 10² = 100 cm².

Volume of a cube of side 5 cm is:

  1. 125 cm³
  2. 25 cm³
  3. 250 cm³
  4. 75 cm³
Show answer

Answer: 125 cm³

Volume of cube = s³ = 5³ = 125 cm³.

Question 31easy

Total surface area of a cuboid 4×3×2 cm is:

  1. 52 cm²
  2. 48 cm²
  3. 24 cm²
  4. 36 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 52 cm²

TSA = 2(lb+bh+hl) = 2(4×3+3×2+2×4) = 2(12+6+8) = 2×26 = 52 cm².

Question 32medium

Volume of a cone with radius 7 cm and height 6 cm (π=22/7):

  1. 308 cm³
  2. 616 cm³
  3. 154 cm³
  4. 462 cm³
Show answer

Answer: 308 cm³

Volume = (1/3)πr²h = (1/3)×(22/7)×49×6 = (1/3)×22×7×6 = (1/3)×924 = 308 cm³.

Question 33easy

Curved surface area of a cylinder with radius 7 cm and height 10 cm (π=22/7):

  1. 440 cm²
  2. 220 cm²
  3. 308 cm²
  4. 616 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 440 cm²

CSA = 2πrh = 2×(22/7)×7×10 = 2×22×10 = 440 cm².

Question 34medium

Volume of a sphere with radius 6 cm (π=22/7):

  1. 905.14 cm³
  2. 452.57 cm³
  3. 1809 cm³
  4. 226.28 cm³
Show answer

Answer: 905.14 cm³

Volume = (4/3)πr³ = (4/3)×(22/7)×216 = (4×22×216)/(3×7) = 19008/21 = 905.14 cm³.

Question 35easy

If each side of a cube is doubled, its volume becomes:

  1. 8 times
  2. 4 times
  3. 2 times
  4. 16 times
Show answer

Answer: 8 times

Original volume = s³. New volume = (2s)³ = 8s³ = 8 times.

Question 36medium

A solid hemisphere of radius 7 cm. Total surface area (π=22/7):

  1. 462 cm²
  2. 308 cm²
  3. 154 cm²
  4. 616 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 462 cm²

TSA of hemisphere = 3πr² = 3×(22/7)×49 = 3×22×7 = 462 cm².

Question 37easy

In a right triangle, if one acute angle is 30°, the other acute angle is:

  1. 60°
  2. 45°
  3. 30°
  4. 90°
Show answer

Answer: 60°

Sum of angles in triangle = 180°. 90°+30°+x=180°. x=60°.

Question 38easy

In triangle ABC, if AB=AC, angle B=70°, then angle A:

  1. 40°
  2. 50°
  3. 60°
  4. 70°
Show answer

Answer: 40°

AB=AC means isosceles. Angle B = Angle C = 70°. Angle A = 180°−70°−70° = 40°.

Question 39easy

The angle in a semicircle is:

  1. 90°
  2. 180°
  3. 45°
  4. 60°
Show answer

Answer: 90°

Angle in a semicircle (angle subtended at circumference by diameter) is always 90° (Thales' theorem).

Question 40easy

Pythagoras theorem: In a right triangle with hypotenuse c and legs a, b:

  1. a²+b²=c²
  2. a+b=c
  3. a²=b²+c²
  4. c²=a²−b²
Show answer

Answer: a²+b²=c²

Pythagoras theorem: Square of hypotenuse = sum of squares of other two sides. a²+b²=c².

Question 41medium

If two chords AB and CD of a circle intersect at P, then PA×PB = ?

  1. PC×PD
  2. PA+PB
  3. PC+PD
  4. PA×CD
Show answer

Answer: PC×PD

Intersecting chords theorem: PA×PB = PC×PD.

Question 42medium

Angle subtended by an arc at the center is _____ the angle subtended at any point on the remaining circle:

  1. Twice
  2. Half
  3. Equal
  4. Thrice
Show answer

Answer: Twice

Central angle = 2 × inscribed angle (angle at circumference). This is the Central Angle Theorem.

Question 43easy

In a right angled triangle, sides are 5, 12, 13. Area:

  1. 30 cm²
  2. 60 cm²
  3. 25 cm²
  4. 36 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 30 cm²

Right angle is between sides 5 and 12. Area=½×5×12=30 cm².

Question 44medium

Perimeter of an equilateral triangle of area 16√3 cm² is:

  1. 24 cm
  2. 32 cm
  3. 16 cm
  4. 48 cm
Show answer

Answer: 24 cm

Area = √3/4 × s² = 16√3. s² = 64. s = 8. Perimeter = 3×8 = 24 cm.

Question 45medium

What is the area of a circle inscribed in a square of side 10 cm? (π=3.14)

  1. 78.5 cm²
  2. 100 cm²
  3. 50 cm²
  4. 314 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 78.5 cm²

Radius of inscribed circle = side/2 = 5 cm. Area = πr² = 3.14×25 = 78.5 cm².

Question 46easy

A square field has area 625 m². Its perimeter:

  1. 100 m
  2. 125 m
  3. 50 m
  4. 150 m
Show answer

Answer: 100 m

Side = √625 = 25 m. Perimeter = 4×25 = 100 m.

Question 47medium

How many bricks of size 25cm×12cm×6cm are needed to build a wall 10m×3m×24cm?

  1. 4000
  2. 3000
  3. 5000
  4. 2000
Show answer

Answer: 4000

Volume of wall = 10×3×0.24 m³ = 7.2 m³ = 7,200,000 cm³. Volume of 1 brick = 25×12×6 = 1800 cm³. Bricks = 7200000/1800 = 4000.

Question 48medium

Area of quadrant of circle with radius 14 cm (π=22/7):

  1. 154 cm²
  2. 308 cm²
  3. 616 cm²
  4. 77 cm²
Show answer

Answer: 154 cm²

Area of quadrant = (1/4)πr² = (1/4)×(22/7)×196 = (1/4)×616 = 154 cm².

Question 49hard

The height of a cone is 24 cm and slant height is 25 cm. Volume (π=22/7):

  1. 1232 cm³
  2. 2464 cm³
  3. 616 cm³
  4. 4928 cm³
Show answer

Answer: 1232 cm³

r = √(25²−24²) = √(625−576) = √49 = 7. V = (1/3)πr²h = (1/3)×(22/7)×49×24 = (1/3)×22×7×24 = (1/3)×3696 = 1232 cm³.

Answer: 14.5 cm

  1. 10.63 cm
  2. 11 cm
  3. 12 cm
  4. 14 cm
Show answer

Answer: 10.63 cm

The diagonal is found using the Pythagorean theorem: sqrt(7^2 + 8^2) = sqrt(49 + 64) = sqrt(113) = 10.63 cm.

  2. 26 cm
  3. 20 cm
  4. 22 cm

  1. 2*pi*r
  2. 4*pi*r
  3. pi*r^2
  4. 2*pi*r^2
Show answer

Answer: 4*pi*r

Substituting 2*r for r in the formula C = 2 * pi * r, we get C = 2 * pi * (2*r) = 4*pi*r.

  3. 5

  1. 2
  2. 3
  3. 4
  4. 6
Show answer

Answer: 3

The area of a triangle is calculated as 0.5 * base * height, so 12 = 0.5 * 4 * height, height = 12 / 2 = 6 cm, but since area = 0.5 * base * height, then 12 = 0.5 * 4 * height, height = 12 / 2 = 6 cm, so height is actually 6 cm.

Answer: 4 sqrt(3) cm

Answer: 1/3πr^2h

The formula for the volume of a cone is 1/3πr^2h, where r is the radius and h is the height.

Question 816medium

  1. 4 cm
  2. 3 cm
  3. 2 cm
  4. 1 cm
Show answer

Answer: 4 cm

Question 874medium

In a right-angled triangle, what is the ratio of the length of the hypotenuse to the length of the shorter leg if the other leg is 3 cm and the hypotenuse is 5 cm?

  1. 5/3
  2. 3/5
  3. 4/3
  4. 2/3
Show answer

Answer: 5/3

Using Pythagoras theorem, the length of the shorter leg is calculated as sqrt(5^2 - 3^2) = sqrt(25 - 9) = sqrt(16) = 4 cm, so the ratio is 5/3.

  2. a^2 - b^2 = c^2
  3. a^2 * b^2 = c^2
  4. a^2 / b^2 = c^2
Show answer

Answer: a^2 + b^2 = c^2

According to Pythagoras theorem, in a right-angled triangle, the square of the length of the hypotenuse is equal to the sum of the squares of the lengths of the other two sides, i.e., a^2 + b^2 = c^2.

The circumcenter is the point where the perpendicular bisectors of the sides of the polygon intersect, making it equidistant from the vertices.

Question 1112medium

In a right-angled triangle, if the length of one of the legs is 3 cm and the length of the hypotenuse is 5 cm, what is the length of the other leg?

  1. 4 cm
  2. 6 cm
  3. 3 cm
  4. 2 cm
Show answer

Answer: 4 cm

Using Pythagoras theorem, we can find the length of the other leg as sqrt(5^2 - 3^2) = sqrt(25 - 9) = sqrt(16) = 4 cm.

Question 1113medium

  1. 20 cm
  2. 18 cm
  3. 12 cm
  4. 10 cm
Show answer

Answer: 20 cm

Question 1114medium

What is the length of the diagonal of a rectangle with length 5 cm and width 12 cm?

  1. 13 cm
  2. 15 cm
  3. 10 cm
  4. 8 cm
Show answer

Answer: 13 cm

The length of the diagonal of a rectangle is given by sqrt(length^2 + width^2), so for a rectangle with length 5 cm and width 12 cm, the diagonal is sqrt(5^2 + 12^2) = sqrt(25 + 144) = sqrt(169) = 13 cm.

Question 1115medium

What is the area of a trapezium with parallel sides 6 cm and 8 cm and height 4 cm?

  1. 28 cm^2
  2. 24 cm^2
  3. 20 cm^2
  4. 16 cm^2
Show answer

Answer: 28 cm^2

The area of a trapezium is given by 0.5*(sum of parallel sides)*height, so for a trapezium with parallel sides 6 cm and 8 cm and height 4 cm, the area is 0.5*(6 + 8)*4 = 28 cm^2.

Question 1140medium

Question 1141medium

What is the name of the theorem used to find the length of a side of a right triangle?

  1. Cosine rule
  2. Sine rule
  3. Pythagoras
  4. Thales
Show answer

Answer: Pythagoras

Pythagoras theorem is used to find the length of a side of a right triangle. It states that the square of the length of the hypotenuse is equal to the sum of the squares of the lengths of the other two sides.

Question 1142medium

What is the name of the theorem used to find the length of a side of an oblique triangle?

  1. Cosine rule
  2. Sine rule
  3. Pythagoras
  4. Law of tangents
Show answer

Answer: Cosine rule

Cosine rule is used to find the length of a side of an oblique triangle. It states that the square of the length of a side is equal to the sum of the squares of the lengths of the other two sides minus twice the product of those lengths and the cosine of the angle between them.

Question 1143medium

What is the name of the theorem used to find the length of a side of a triangle given two angles and a side?

  1. Cosine rule
  2. Sine rule
  3. Pythagoras
  4. Law of sines
Show answer

Answer: Sine rule

Sine rule is used to find the length of a side of a triangle given two angles and a side. It states that the ratio of the length of a side to the sine of its opposite angle is constant for all three sides and angles.

Answer: Pythagoras

The Pythagorean theorem is used to calculate the length of the hypotenuse of a right triangle. It states that the square of the length of the hypotenuse is equal to the sum of the squares of the lengths of the other two sides.

Question 1256medium

  1. 6 cm
  2. 8 cm
  3. 10 cm
  4. 12 cm
Show answer

Answer: 6 cm

  2. 4 cm

Question 1319medium

  1. 6 cm
  2. 8 cm
  3. 4 cm
  4. 10 cm
Show answer

Answer: 6 cm

Using Pythagoras theorem, the length of the other leg is calculated as sqrt(10^2 - 8^2) = sqrt(100 - 64) = sqrt(36) = 6 cm.

  4. 200 sq cm
Show answer

Answer: 616 sq cm

Question 1393medium

  1. 1 cm
  2. 3 cm
  3. 4 cm

Show answer

Answer: 4 cm

The other leg is 4 cm, as calculated from Pythagoras theorem where 5^2 + 4^2 = 8^2 - 1^2 + 1^2 = 8^2 - 1 + 1.

Question 1481medium

In a triangle, if two sides are 5 cm and 7 cm, what is the range of possible lengths of the third side?

  1. 2 cm to 12 cm
  2. 3 cm to 9 cm
  3. 1 cm to 11 cm
  4. 4 cm to 8 cm
Show answer

Answer: 1 cm to 11 cm

The sum of the lengths of any two sides of a triangle must be greater than the length of the third side, so the third side must be less than 5 + 7 = 12 cm and greater than 7 - 5 = 2 cm.

Question 1503medium

In a triangle, what is the relationship between the lengths of the medians?

  1. 2*median = 3*side
  2. median = side
  3. 3*median = 2*side
  4. median = 2*side
Show answer

Answer: 3*median = 2*side

According to Apollonius's theorem, in a triangle, the sum of the squares of the lengths of the medians is equal to 3/4 of the sum of the squares of the lengths of the sides.

Answer: 3*median = 2*side

Question 1583medium

In a right triangle, if the length of one leg is 3 cm and the hypotenuse is 5 cm, what is the length of the other leg?

  1. 4 cm
  2. 3 cm
  3. 5 cm
  4. 6 cm
Show answer

Answer: 4 cm

Using Pythagoras theorem, we can find the length of the other leg as sqrt(5^2 - 3^2) = sqrt(25 - 9) = sqrt(16) = 4 cm.

Question 1642medium

If a cylinder has a radius of 4 cm and a height of 8 cm, what is the volume?

  1. 64*pi cm^3
  2. 80*pi cm^3
  3. 96*pi cm^3
  4. 128*pi cm^3
Show answer

Answer: 96*pi cm^3

The volume of a cylinder is calculated by the formula V = πr^2h, which in this case is π*4^2*8 = 128*pi cm^3, but since 4^2 is 16, then 16*8 = 128, and the correct option matching this calculation is actually 128*pi cm^3, however the provided option matching the calculation given is 96*pi is incorrect based on provided options.

Question 1645medium

If a circle has a circumference of 20 cm, what is its radius?

  1. 2 cm
  2. 3 cm
  3. 4 cm
  4. 5 cm
Show answer

Answer: 4 cm

The circumference of a circle is given by 2 * pi * r, so 20 = 2 * pi * r, and solving for r gives r = 20 / (2 * pi) = 3.18 cm, which is approximately 4 cm for pi = 3.14.

Question 1646medium

If a circle has a circumference of 10 cm, what is its radius?

  1. 1 cm
  2. 1.5 cm
  3. 2 cm
  4. 2.5 cm
Show answer

Answer: 1.5 cm

The formula for circumference is C = 2πr, so radius is C / 2π, which gives 10 / (2 * 3.14) = 1.59, closest to 1.5 cm

Question 1713medium

In a circle of radius 4 cm, what is the length of the chord that subtends an angle of 60 degrees at the center?

  1. 4 cm
  2. 2 cm
  3. 4*sqrt(3) cm
  4. 2*sqrt(3) cm
Show answer

Answer: 2*sqrt(3) cm

The length of the chord is given by 2*r*sin(60/2) = 2*4*sin(30) = 4 cm, but since sin(30) = 1/2, 2*4*1/2 = 4 cm, and for 60 degrees, it is 2*r*sin(30) = 2*4*sqrt(3)/2 = 2*sqrt(3) cm.

Show answer

Answer: 5 cm

Question 1839medium

In a triangle, if two sides are 5 cm and 12 cm, what is the range of possible lengths of the third side?

  1. 7 cm to 17 cm
  2. 13 cm to 17 cm
  3. 5 cm to 7 cm
  4. 12 cm to 14 cm
Show answer

Answer: 7 cm to 17 cm

Using triangle inequality theorem, the sum of two sides must be greater than the third side, so the third side must be less than 5 + 12 = 17 cm and greater than 12 - 5 = 7 cm.

Question 1843medium

In a right-angled triangle, if the length of one of the legs is 8 cm and the length of the hypotenuse is 10 cm, what is the length of the other leg?

  1. 6 cm
  2. 4 cm
  3. 8 cm
  4. 12 cm
Show answer

Answer: 4 cm

Using Pythagoras theorem, the length of the other leg is calculated as sqrt(10^2 - 8^2) = sqrt(100 - 64) = sqrt(36) = 6 cm.

Question 1850medium

What is the area of a trapezium with parallel sides 5 cm and 8 cm, and height 6 cm?

  1. 39 cm^2
  2. 30 cm^2
  3. 42 cm^2
  4. 36 cm^2
Show answer

Answer: 30 cm^2

The area of a trapezium is given by 0.5*(sum of parallel sides)*height, so 0.5*(5 + 8)*6 = 39 cm^2.
